PROBLEM   The  series  sum  of  1/(k(k+2)),  k  up  to  8,  equals  m/n  reduced.  Find  m+n.  
---  rollout  0   (graded  CORRECT)  --- 
To  solve  the  given  problem,  we  first  need  to  simplify  the  general  term  of  the  series  \(  
\frac{1}{k(k+2)}
 
\).
 
 
We
 
can
 
use
 
partial
 
fraction
 
decomposition:
 
\[
 
\frac{1}{k(k+2)}
 
=
 
\frac{A}{k}
 
+
 
\frac{B}{k+2}
 
\]
 
Multiplying
 
both
 
sides
 
by
 
\(
 
k(k+2)
 
\)
 
gives:
 
\[
 
1
 
=
 
A(k+2)
 
+
 
Bk
 
\]
 
Expanding
 
and
 
combining
 
like
 
terms,
 
we
 
get:
 
\[
 
1
 
=
 
Ak
 
+
 
2A
 
+
 
Bk
 
\]
 
\[
 
1
 
=
 
(A+B)k
 
+
 
2A
 
\]
 
For
 
this
 
equation
 
to
 
hold
 
for
 
all
 
\(
 
k
 
\),
 
the
 
coefficients
 
of
 
\(
 
k
 
\)
 
must
 
be
 
equal
 
on
 
both
 
sides,
 
giving
 
us
 
two
 
equations:
 
\[
 
A
 
+
 
B
 
=
 
0
 
\]
 
\[
 
2A
 
=
 
1
 
\]
 
Solving
 
these,
 
we
 
find:
 
\[
 
A
 
=
 
\frac{1}{2},
 
\quad
 
B
 
=
 
-\frac{1}{2}
 
\]
 
So,
 
we
 
have:
 
\[
 
\frac{1}{k(k+2)}
 
=
 
\frac{1/2}{k}
 
-
 
\frac{1/2}{k+2}
 
=
 
\frac{1}{2}
 
\left(
 
\frac{1}{k}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{k+2}
 
\right)
 
\]
 
 
Now
 
we
 
can
 
write
 
the
 
series
 
as:
 
\[
 
\sum_{k=1}^8
 
\frac{1}{k(k+2)}
 
=
 
\sum_{k=1}^8
 
\frac{1}{2}
 
\left(
 
\frac{1}{k}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{k+2}
 
\right)
 
=
 
\frac{1}{2}
 
\sum_{k=1}^8
 
\left(
 
\frac{1}{k}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{k+2}
 
\right)
 
\]
 
 
This
 
is
 
a
 
telescoping
 
series.
 
Writing
 
out
 
the
 
first
 
few
 
terms,
 
we
 
get:
 
\[
 
\frac{1}{2}
 
\left(
 
\left(
 
\frac{1}{1}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{3}
 
\right)
 
+
 
\left(
 
\frac{1}{2}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{4}
 
\right)
 
+
 
\left(
 
\frac{1}{3}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{5}
 
\right)
 
+
 
\left(
 
\frac{1}{4}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{6}
 
\right)
 
+
 
\left(
 
\frac{1}{5}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{7}
 
\right)
 
+
 
\left(
 
\frac{1}{6}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{8}
 
\right)
 
+
 
\left(
 
\frac{1}{7}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{9}
 
\right)
 
+
 
\left(
 
\frac{1}{8}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{10}
 
\right)
 
\right)
 
\]
 
 
Notice
 
that
 
most
 
terms
 
cancel
 
out,
 
leaving:
 
\[
 
\frac{1}{2}
 
\left(
 
1
 
+
 
\frac{1}{2}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{9}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{10}
 
\right)
 
\]
 
Simplifying
 
inside
 
the
 
parentheses:
 
\[
 
1
 
+
 
\frac{1}{2}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{9}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{10}
 
=
 
\frac{180}{180}
 
+
 
\frac{90}{180}
 
-
 
\frac{20}{180}
 
-
 
\frac{18}{180}
 
=
 
\frac{232}{180}
 
=
 
\frac{116}{90}
 
=
 
\frac{58}{45}
 
\]
 
Thus,
 
the
 
sum
 
is:
 
\[
 
\frac{1}{2}
 
\cdot
 
\frac{58}{45}
 
=
 
\frac{58}{90}
 
=
 
\frac{29}{45}
 
\]
 
 
The
 
fraction
 
\(
 
\frac{29}{45}
 
\)
 
is
 
already
 
in
 
its
 
simplest
 
form,
 
so
 
\(
 
m
 
=
 
29
 
\)
 
and
 
\(  n  =  45  \).  Therefore,  \(  m+n  =  29+45  =  74  \).  
 
The
 
answer
 
is:
 
\[
 
\boxed{74}

=
 
\frac{1}{2}
 
\sum_{k=1}^{8}
 
\left(
 
\frac{1}{k}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{k+2}
 
\right)
 
\]

is
 
a

\[

\frac{1}{5}
 
\right)

\left(
 
\frac{1}{8}

\frac{1}{10}
 
\right)
 
\right)
 
\]

\[
 
\frac{1}{2}
 
\left(

\frac{1}{2}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{9}
 
-
 
\frac{1}{10}
 
\right)
 
\]

\frac{1}{2}

\frac{3}{2}
 
\]
 
\[

-
 
\frac{1}{10}

-\left(
 
\frac{10
 
+
 
9}{90}
 
\right)
 
=
 
-\frac{19}{90}
 
\]

\[

\left(
 
\frac{3}{2}
 
-
 
\frac{19}{90}
 
\right)
 
\]

\[
 
\frac{3}{2}
 
=
 
\frac{135}{90}
 
\]
 
\[
 
\frac{135}{90}

\frac{19}{90}
 
=
 
\frac{116}{90}
 
=
 
\frac{58}{45}
 
\]

series
 
sum

\frac{58}{45}
 
=
 
\frac{58}{90}
 
=
 
\frac{29}{45}
 
\]

fraction
 
\(
 
\frac{29}{45}

is
 
already
 
in
 
its
 
simplest
 
form.

\(

\(

\).

PROBLEM   The  series  sum  of  1/(k(k+3)),  k  up  to  6,  equals  m/n  reduced.  Find  m+n.  
---  rollout  0   (graded  WRONG)  ---

decomposing
 
the
 
general
 
term
 
using
 
partial
 
fractions.
 
We
 
want
 
to

\(\frac{1}{k(k+3)}\)
 
in

\[

\frac{B}{k+3}
 
\]
 
 
Multiplying  both  sides  by  \(k(k+3)\)  gives:

The

of
 
divisors
 
of
 
a

\(

p_2^{e_2}

(e_k

\(

\(

\times

\(

\).

PROBLEM   How  many  integers  from  2000  to  2999  have  digits  summing  to  exactly  12?  
---  rollout  0   (graded  WRONG)  --- 
To  determine  how  many  integers  from  2000  to  2999  have  digits  summing  to  exactly  12,  we  
start
 
by
 
expressing
 
these
 
numbers
 
in
 
the
 
form
 
\(2abc\),
 
where
 
\(a,
 
b,\)
 
and
 
\(c\)
 
are
 
the
 
digits
 
of
 
the
 
number.
 
The
 
equation
 
we
 
need
 
to
 
solve
 
is:
 
 
\[2
 
+
 
a
 
+
 
b
 
+
 
c
 
=
 
12.\]
 
 
Subtracting
 
2
 
from
 
both
 
sides,
 
we
 
get:
 
 
\[a
 
+
 
b
 
+
 
c
 
=
 
10.\]
 
 
We
 
need
 
to
 
find
 
the
 
number
 
of
 
non-negative
 
integer
 
solutions
 
to
 
this
 
equation.
 
This
 
is
 
a
 
classic
 
"stars
 
and
 
bars"
 
problem
 
in
 
combinatorics.
 
The
 
formula
 
for
 
the
 
number
 
of
 
non-negative
 
integer
 
solutions
 
to
 
the
 
equation
 
\(x_1
 
+
 
x_2
 
+
 
\cdots
 
+
 
x_k
 
=
 
n\)
 
is
 
given
 
by
 
\(\binom{n+k-1}{k-1}\).
 
Here,
 
\(n
 
=
 
10\)
 
and
 
\(k
 
=
 
3\),
 
so
 
we
 
need
 
to
 
calculate
 
\(\binom{10+3-1}{3-1}
 
=
 
\binom{12}{2}\).
 
 
The
 
binomial
 
coefficient
 
\(\binom{12}{2}\)
 
is
 
calculated
 
as
 
follows:
 
 
\[
 
\binom{12}{2}
 
=
 
\frac{12
 
\times
 
11}{2
 
\times
 
1}
 
=
 
66.
 
\]
 
 
Thus,
 
there
 
are
 
66
 
integers
 
from
 
2000
 
to
 
2999
 
whose
 
digits
 
sum
 
to
 
exactly

start
 
by
 
noting
 
that
 
any
 
number
 
in
 
this
 
range
 
can
 
be
 
represented
 
as
 
\(2abc\),
 
where
 
\(a\),
 
\(b\),
 
and
 
\(c\)
 
are
 
the
 
hundreds,
 
tens,
 
and
 
units
 
digits
 
respectively.
 
The
 
condition
 
is
 
that
 
the
 
sum
 
of
 
these
 
digits
 
must
 
equal
 
12,
 
i.e.,
 
\(2
 
+
 
a
 
+
 
b
 
+
 
c
 
=
 
12\).
 
Simplifying,
 
we
 
get:
 
\[a
 
+
 
b
 
+
 
c
 
=
 
10.\]
 
 
We
 
need
 
to
 
find
 
the
 
number
 
of
 
non-negative
 
integer
 
solutions
 
to
 
this
 
equation.
 
This
 
is
 
a
 
classic
 
"stars
 
and
 
bars"
 
problem,
 
where
 
the
 
number
 
of
 
solutions
 
is
 
given
 
by
 
the
 
binomial
 
coefficient
 
\(\binom{n+r-1}{r-1}\),
 
where
 
\(n\)
 
is
 
the
 
total
 
sum
 
(10)
 
and
 
\(r\)
 
is
 
the
 
number
 
of
 
variables
 
(3).
 
 
Here,
 
we
 
have:
 
\[
 
\binom{10+3-1}{3-1}
 
=
 
\binom{12}{2}.
 
\]
 
 
Calculating
 
the
 
binomial
 
coefficient,
 
we
 
get:
 
\[
 
\binom{12}{2}
 
=
 
\frac{12
 
\times
 
11}{2
 
\times
 
1}
 
=
 
66.
 
\]
 
 
Therefore,
 
the
 
number
 
of
 
integers
 
from
 
2000
 
to
 
2999
 
that
 
have
 
digits
 
summing
 
to
 
exactly
 
12
 
is
 
\(\boxed{66}\).

22
 
\implies
 
a'
 
+
 
b'
 
+
 
c'
 
=
 
19.
 
   
\]
 
   
Now,
 
we
 
need
 
to
 
find
 
the
 
number
 
of
 
solutions
 
to
 
\(a'
 
+
 
b'
 
+
 
c'
 
=
 
19\)
 
where
 
\(a',
 
b',
 
c'\)
 
are
 
non-negative
 
integers.
 
 
2.

the
 
solutions
 
using
 
combinatorics**:

number
 
of
 
non-negative
 
integer
 
solutions
 
to
 
the
 
equation
 
\(a'
 
+
 
b'
 
+
 
c'
 
=

is
 
given
 
by
 
the
 
"stars
 
and
 
bars"

The
 
formula
 
for

number
 
of
 
solutions
 
is:
 
   
\[
 
   
\binom{19
 
+
 
3
 
-
 
1}{3
 
-
 
1}
 
=
 
\binom{21}{2}.
 
   
\]
 
   
Calculating
 
this,
 
we
 
get:
 
   
\[
 
   \binom{21}{2}  =  \frac{21  \times  20}{2  \times  1}  =  210.  
   
\]
 
 
Therefore,
 
the
 
number
 
of
 
ordered

\((a,

such

\(0
 
\leq

<

<

+

is
 
\(\boxed{210}\).

PROBLEM   Of  the  divisors  of  720,  how  many  are  odd?  
---  rollout  0   (graded  CORRECT)  --- 
To  determine  how  many  divisors  of  720  are  odd,  we  first  need  to  find  the  prime  
factorization
 
of
 
720.
 
We
 
can
 
do
 
this
 
as
 
follows:
 
 
\[
 
720
 
=
 
72
 
\times
 
10
 
=
 
(8
 
\times
 
9)
 
\times
 
(2
 
\times
 
5)
 
=
 
(2^3
 
\times
 
3^2)
 
\times
 
(2
 
\times
 
5)
 
=
 
2^4
 
\times
 
3^2
 
\times
 
5
 
\]
 
 
The
 
prime
 
factorization
 
of
 
720
 
is
 
\(2^4
 
\times
 
3^2
 
\times
 
5\).
 
To
 
find
 
the
 
number
 
of
 
odd
 
divisors,
 
we
 
ignore
 
the
 
factor
 
of
 
2
 
and
 
focus
 
only
 
on
 
the
 
factors
 
of
 
\(3^2
 
\times
 
5\).
 
 
The
 
number
 
of
 
divisors
 
of
 
a
 
number
 
\(p^a
 
\times
 
q^b
 
\times
 
r^c
 
\times
 
\cdots\)
 
is
 
given
 
by
 
\((a+1)(b+1)(c+1)\cdots\).
 
Applying
 
this
 
to
 
\(3^2
 
\times
 
5^1\),
 
we
 
get:
 
 
\[  (2+1)(1+1)  =  3  \times  2  =  6  \]  
 
Thus,
 
the
 
number
 
of
 
odd
 
divisors
 
of
 
720
 
is
 
\(\boxed{6}\).
 
 
To
 
verify,
 
we
 
can
 
list
 
all
 
the
 
odd
 
divisors
 
of
 
720.
 
They
 
are:
 
1,
 
3,
 
5,
 
9,
 
15,
 
and
 
45.
 
There
 
are
 
indeed
 
6
 
odd
 
divisors.

rolled
 
so
 
that
 
the
 
probability
 
of
 
a
 
specific
 
face
 
appearing
 
at

exceeds
 
\(
 
\frac{3}{4}
 
\).

\(

\)
 
as

of

-
 
\(

as

a

\(

\[

\frac{1}{8}
 
\]

of
 
not
 
rolling
 
a
 
specific
 
face
 
on

is:
 
\[
 
1
 
-

=
 
1
 
-
 
\frac{1}{8}

\frac{7}{8}
 
\]

\(

not

the

\right)^n

specific
 
face
 
at

in
 
\(

\)
 
rolls

\[
 
1
 
-
 
\left(
 
\frac{7}{8}
 
\right)^n
 
\]

to
 
be

than
 
\(
 
\frac{3}{4}
 
\):
 
\[

\left(
 
\frac{7}{8}
 
\right)^n
 
>
 
\frac{3}{4}

\(
 
\frac{3}{4}

to

\[  1  -  \frac{3}{4}  >  \left(  \frac{7}{8}  \right)^n  \]

\frac{1}{4}
 
>
 
\left(
 
\frac{7}{8}
 
\right)^n
 
\]

\(

\left(

\right)

\ln

\right)

=
